href="/wiki/Qasr_El_Nil_Bridge" title="Qasr El Nil Bridge">Qasr El Nil Bridge</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CH-NB_-_Aegypten,_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3471" data-file-width="4642" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif/lossy-page1-220px-CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif/lossy-page1-330px-CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif/lossy-page1-440px-CH-NB_-_Aegypten%2C_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CH-NB_-_Aegypten,_Kairo_und_Nil_-_Eduard_Spelterini_-_EAD-WEHR-32043-B.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view 1904 from a balloon where the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Egyptian Museum</a> appears to the right side.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2741" data-file-width="4501" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Panorama_1950%27s.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panoramic view of Cairo, 1950s</div></div></div>
<p>Until his death in 1848, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali Pasha</a> instituted a number of social and economic reforms that earned him the title of founder of modern Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfaf_Lutfi_Sayyid-Marsot19841_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfaf_Lutfi_Sayyid-Marsot19841-113">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGregor200653_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGregor200653-114">[112]</a></sup> However, while Muhammad Ali initiated the construction of public buildings in the city,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShillington2005437_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShillington2005437-115">[113]</a></sup> those reforms had minimal effect on Cairo's landscape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000291,_302_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000291,_302-116">[114]</a></sup> Bigger changes came to Cairo under <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma'il Pasha">Isma'il Pasha</a> (r. 1863–1879), who continued the modernisation processes started by his grandfather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> Drawing inspiration from <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, Isma'il envisioned a city of <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">maidans</a> and wide avenues; due to financial constraints, only some of them, in the area now composing <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cairo" title="Downtown Cairo">Downtown Cairo</a>, came to fruition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000313–314_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000313–314-118">[116]</a></sup> Isma'il also sought to modernize the city, which was merging with neighbouring settlements, by establishing a <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">public works</a> ministry, bringing <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> and lighting to the city, and opening a theatre and opera house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000311–313_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000311–313-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965436–444_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965436–444-120">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>The immense debt resulting from Isma'il's projects provided a pretext for increasing European control, which culminated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1882_Anglo-Egyptian_War" title="1882 Anglo-Egyptian War">British invasion</a> in 1882.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShillington2005199_83-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShillington2005199-83">[81]</a></sup> The city's economic centre quickly moved west toward the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>, away from the historic <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a> section and toward the contemporary, European-style areas built by Isma'il.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965429–431,_455–457_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965429–431,_455–457-121">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHouraniKhouryWilson2004317_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHouraniKhouryWilson2004317-122">[120]</a></sup> Europeans accounted for five percent of Cairo's population at the end of the 19th century, by which point they held most top governmental positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965431_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbu-Lughod1965431-123">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1906 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cairo_Electric_Railways_%26_Heliopolis_Oases_Company" title="Cairo Electric Railways &amp; Heliopolis Oases Company">Heliopolis Oasis Company</a> headed by the <a href="/wiki/Belgians" title="Belgians">Belgian</a> industrialist <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_Empain" title="Édouard Empain">Édouard Empain</a> and his Egyptian counterpart <a href="/wiki/Boghos_Nubar" title="Boghos Nubar">Boghos Nubar</a>, built a suburb called <a href="/wiki/Heliopolis,_Cairo" title="Heliopolis, Cairo">Heliopolis</a> (city of the sun in Greek) ten kilometers from the center of Cairo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000329_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000329-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEElyachar200556_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEElyachar200556-125">[123]</a></sup> It represented the first large-scale attempt to promote its own architecture, known now as the <a href="/wiki/Heliopolis_style" title="Heliopolis style">Heliopolis style</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title='Not at all clear that "Heliopolis style" is a common term used in any publications. Please provide reliable source(s) or revise to avoid stating original research. (June 2022)'>citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1905–1907 the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Gezira_(Cairo)" title="Gezira (Cairo)">Gezira</a> island was developed by the Baehler Company into <a href="/wiki/Zamalek" title="Zamalek">Zamalek</a>, which would later become Cairo's upscale "chic" neighbourhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000328_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000328-126">[124]</a></sup> In 1906 construction began on Garden City, a neighbourhood of urban villas with gardens and curved streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000328_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000328-126">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British occupation was intended to be temporary, but it lasted well into the 20th century. Nationalists staged <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1919" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1919">large-scale demonstrations</a> in Cairo in 1919,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShillington2005199_83-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShillington2005199-83">[81]</a></sup> five years after Egypt had been declared a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHouraniKhouryWilson200412_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHouraniKhouryWilson200412-127">[125]</a></sup> Nevertheless, this led to Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Unilateral_Declaration_of_Egyptian_Independence" title="Unilateral Declaration of Egyptian Independence">independence in 1922</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1924_Cairo_Quran">1924 Cairo Quran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1924 Cairo Quran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Fuad_I_Edition" title="King Fuad I Edition">King Fuad I Edition</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qur%27an" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> was first published on 10 July 1924 in Cairo under the patronage of <a href="/wiki/Fuad_I_of_Egypt" title="Fuad I of Egypt">King Fuad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malay_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-malay-130">[128]</a></sup> The goal of the government of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="Kingdom of Egypt">Kingdom of Egypt</a> was not to delegitimize the other variant Quranic texts ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qira%27at" title="Qira'at">qira'at</a>"), but to eliminate errors found in Qur'anic texts used in state schools. A committee of teachers chose to preserve a single one of the canonical qira'at "readings", namely that of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%E1%B8%A4af%E1%B9%A3" title="Ḥafṣ">Ḥafṣ</a>" version,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBöwering200874_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBöwering200874-131">[129]</a></sup> an 8th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kufic_recitation" title="Kufic recitation">Kufic recitation</a>. This edition has become the standard for modern printings of the Quran<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rippin_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-rippin-132">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melchert2_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-melchert2-133">[131]</a></sup> for much of the Islamic world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The publication has been called a "terrific success", and the edition has been described as one "now widely seen as the official text of the Qur'an", so popular among both Sunni and Shi'a that the common belief among less well-informed Muslims is "that the Qur'an has a single, unambiguous reading". Minor amendments were made later in 1924 and in 1936 - the "Faruq edition" in honour of then ruler, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Faruq" title="King Faruq">King Faruq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds20082_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds20082-135">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="British_occupation_until_1956">British occupation until 1956</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: British occupation until 1956">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2656" data-file-width="4479" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Street_1950%27s.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Everyday life in Cairo, 1950s</div></div></div>
<p>British troops remained in the country until 1956. During this time, urban Cairo, spurred by new bridges and transport links, continued to expand to include the upscale neighbourhoods of Garden City, Zamalek, and Heliopolis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000326–329_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000326–329-136">[134]</a></sup> Between 1882 and 1937, the population of Cairo more than tripled—from 347,000 to 1.3 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000319_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000319-137">[135]</a></sup>—and its area increased from 10 to 163 km<sup>2</sup> (4 to 63 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000322_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000322-138">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city was devastated during the 1952 riots known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cairo_Fire" title="Cairo Fire">Cairo Fire</a> or Black Saturday, which saw the destruction of nearly 700 shops, movie theatres, casinos and hotels in downtown Cairo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> The British departed Cairo following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">Egyptian Revolution of 1952</a>, but the city's rapid growth showed no signs of abating. Seeking to accommodate the increasing population, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Egypt" title="President of Egypt">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a> redeveloped <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a> and the Nile <a href="/wiki/Corniche" title="Corniche">Corniche</a>, and improved the city's network of bridges and highways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000349_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000349-140">[138]</a></sup> Meanwhile, additional controls of the Nile fostered development within Gezira Island and along the city's waterfront. The metropolis began to encroach on the fertile <a href="/wiki/Nile_Delta" title="Nile Delta">Nile Delta</a>, prompting the government to build desert <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_town" title="Satellite town">satellite towns</a> and devise incentives for city-dwellers to move to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond2000343–345_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond2000343–345-141">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="After_1956">After 1956</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: After 1956">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the second half of the 20th century Cairo continue to grow enormously in both population and area. Between 1947 and 2006 the population of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cairo" title="Greater Cairo">Greater Cairo</a> went from 2,986,280 to 16,292,269.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESims201283_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESims201283-142">[140]</a></sup> The population explosion also drove the rise of "informal" housing (<i>'ashwa'iyyat</i>), meaning housing that was built without any official planning or control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESims201295_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESims201295-143">[141]</a></sup> The exact form of this type of housing varies considerably but usually has a much higher population density than formal housing. By 2009, over 63% of the population of Greater Cairo lived in informal neighbourhoods, even though these occupied only 17% of the total area of Greater Cairo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESims201296_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESims201296-144">[142]</a></sup> According to economist David Sims, informal housing has the benefits of providing affordable accommodation and vibrant communities to huge numbers of Cairo's working classes, but it also suffers from government neglect, a relative lack of services, and overcrowding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESims2012120–122_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESims2012120–122-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>The "formal" city was also expanded. The most notable example was the creation of <a href="/wiki/Nasr_City" title="Nasr City">Madinat Nasr</a>, a huge government-sponsored expansion of the city to the east which officially began in 1959 but was primarily developed in the mid-1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESims201252–53_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESims201252–53-146">[144]</a></sup> Starting in 1977 the Egyptian government established the New Urban Communities Authority to initiate and direct the development of new planned cities on the outskirts of Cairo, generally established on desert land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> These new satellite cities were intended to provide housing, investment, and employment opportunities for the region's growing population as well as to pre-empt the further growth of informal neighbourhoods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-147">[145]</a></sup> As of 2014, about 10% of the population of Greater Cairo lived in the new cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-147">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>Concurrently, Cairo established itself as a political and economic hub for <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, with many multinational businesses and organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, operating out of the city. In 1979 the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">historic districts</a> of Cairo were listed as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-14">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992, Cairo was hit by an <a href="/wiki/1992_Cairo_earthquake" title="1992 Cairo earthquake">earthquake</a> causing 545 deaths, injuring 6,512 and leaving around 50,000 people homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NGDC_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-NGDC-150">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Egyptian_revolution">2011 Egyptian revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2011 Egyptian revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_revolution_of_2011" title="Egyptian revolution of 2011">Egyptian revolution of 2011</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_(Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge)-edit2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2013" data-file-width="1557" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg/170px-The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg/255px-The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg/340px-The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_%28Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge%29-edit2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_lion_of_Egyptian_revolution_(Qasr_al-Nil_Bridge)-edit2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A protester holding an Egyptian flag during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_revolution_of_2011" title="Egyptian revolution of 2011">protests</a> that started on 25 January 2011.</div></div></div><p>Cairo's <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a> was the focal point of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Egyptian_Revolution" title="2011 Egyptian Revolution">2011 Egyptian Revolution</a> against former president <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> Over 2 million protesters were at Cairo's Tahrir square. More than 50,000 protesters first occupied the square on 25 January, during which the area's wireless services were reported to be impaired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Egyptians_report_poor_communication_services_on_Day_of_Anger_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Egyptians_report_poor_communication_services_on_Day_of_Anger-152">[150]</a></sup> In the following days Tahrir Square continued to be the primary destination for protests in Cairo<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> as it took place following a popular uprising that began on Tuesday, 25 January 2011 and continued until June 2013. The uprising was mainly a campaign of non-violent civil resistance, which featured a series of demonstrations, marches, acts of civil disobedience, and labour strikes. Millions of protesters from a variety of socio-economic and religious backgrounds demanded the overthrow of the regime of Egyptian President Hosni Mubarak. Despite being predominantly peaceful in nature, the revolution was not without violent clashes between security forces and protesters, with at least 846 people killed and 6,000 injured. The uprising took place in Cairo, Alexandria, and in other cities in Egypt, following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tunisian_revolution" title="Tunisian revolution">Tunisian revolution</a> that resulted in the overthrow of the long-time <a href="/wiki/President_of_Tunisia" title="President of Tunisia">Tunisian president</a> <a href="/wiki/Zine_El_Abidine_Ben_Ali" title="Zine El Abidine Ben Ali">Zine El Abidine Ben Ali</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> On 11 February, following weeks of determined popular protest and pressure, Hosni Mubarak resigned from office.
</p><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-revolutionary_Cairo">Post-revolutionary Cairo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Post-revolutionary Cairo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Under the rule of President <a href="/wiki/Abdel_Fattah_el-Sisi" title="Abdel Fattah el-Sisi">el-Sisi</a>, in March 2015 plans were announced for another yet-unnamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planned_city" title="Planned city">planned city</a> to be built further east of the existing satellite city of <a href="/wiki/New_Cairo" title="New Cairo">New Cairo</a>, intended to serve as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proposed_new_capital_of_Egypt" title="Proposed new capital of Egypt">new capital of Egypt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_new_capital_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_new_capital-155">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Nile_River.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Cairo_Nile_River.jpg/220px-Cairo_Nile_River.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Cairo_Nile_River.jpg/330px-Cairo_Nile_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Cairo_Nile_River.jpg/440px-Cairo_Nile_River.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Nile_River.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The river <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> flows through Cairo, here contrasting ancient customs of daily life with the modern city of today.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zamalek_Arial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="251" data-file-width="364" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Zamalek_Arial.jpg/220px-Zamalek_Arial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Zamalek_Arial.jpg/330px-Zamalek_Arial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Zamalek_Arial.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zamalek_Arial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view looking south, with the <a href="/wiki/Zamalek" title="Zamalek">Zamalek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gezira_(Cairo)" title="Gezira (Cairo)">Gezira</a> districts on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gezira_Island" title="Gezira Island">Gezira Island</a>, surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg/220px-Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg/330px-Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg/440px-Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_SPOT_1006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cairo seen from <a href="/wiki/SPOT_(satellite)" title="SPOT (satellite)">Spot Satellite</a></div></div></div>
<p>Cairo is located in northern <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Lower_Egypt" title="Lower Egypt">Lower Egypt</a>, 165 km (100 mi) south of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and 120 km (75 mi) west of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Suez" title="Gulf of Suez">Gulf of Suez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> The city lies along the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile River</a>, immediately south of the point where the river leaves its desert-bound valley and branches into the low-lying <a href="/wiki/Nile_Delta" title="Nile Delta">Nile Delta</a> region. Although the Cairo metropolis extends away from the Nile in all directions, the city of Cairo resides only on the east bank of the river and two islands within it on a total area of 453 km<sup>2</sup> (175 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypop_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-citypop-158">[156]</a></sup> Geologically, Cairo lies on <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">alluvium</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sand_dune" title="Sand dune">sand dunes</a> which date from the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">quaternary</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>Until the mid-19th century, when the river was tamed by dams, levees, and other controls, the Nile in the vicinity of Cairo was highly susceptible to changes in course and surface level. Over the years, the Nile gradually shifted westward, providing the site between the eastern edge of the river and the <a href="/wiki/Mokattam" title="Mokattam">Mokattam</a> highlands on which the city now stands. The land on which Cairo was established in 969 (present-day <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a>) was located underwater just over three hundred years earlier, when <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">Fustat</a> was first built.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2002125_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2002125-161">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>Low periods of the Nile during the 11th century continued to add to the landscape of Cairo; a new island, known as <i>Geziret al-Fil</i>, first appeared in 1174, but eventually became connected to the mainland. Today, the site of <i>Geziret al-Fil</i> is occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Shubra" title="Shubra">Shubra</a> district. The low periods created another island at the turn of the 14th century that now composes <a href="/wiki/Zamalek" title="Zamalek">Zamalek</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gezira_Island" title="Gezira Island">Gezira</a>. <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">Land reclamation</a> efforts by the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a> further contributed to expansion on the east bank of the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2002126_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2002126-162">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because of the Nile's movement, the newer parts of the city—<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garden_City_(Cairo)" title="Garden City (Cairo)">Garden City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cairo" title="Downtown Cairo">Downtown Cairo</a>, and Zamalek—are located closest to the riverbank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riverbank_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-riverbank-163">[161]</a></sup> The areas, which are home to most of Cairo's <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_mission" title="Diplomatic mission">embassies</a>, are surrounded on the north, east, and south by the older parts of the city. <a href="/wiki/Old_Cairo" title="Old Cairo">Old Cairo</a>, located south of the centre, holds the remnants of <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">Fustat</a> and the heart of Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church" title="Coptic Orthodox Church">Coptic Christian</a> community, <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Cairo" title="Coptic Cairo">Coptic Cairo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boulaq" title="Boulaq">Boulaq</a> district, which lies in the northern part of the city, was born out of a major 16th-century port and is now a major industrial centre. The Citadel is located east of the city centre around <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a>, which dates back to the Fatimid era and the foundation of Cairo. While western Cairo is dominated by wide boulevards, open spaces, and <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modern architecture</a> of European influence, the eastern half, having grown haphazardly over the centuries, is dominated by small lanes, crowded tenements, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a>.
</p><p>Northern and extreme eastern parts of Cairo, which include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satellite_town" title="Satellite town">satellite towns</a>, are among the most recent additions to the city, as they developed in the late-20th and early-21st centuries to accommodate the city's rapid growth. The western bank of the Nile is commonly included within the urban area of Cairo, but it composes the city of <a href="/wiki/Giza" title="Giza">Giza</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Giza_Governorate" title="Giza Governorate">Giza Governorate</a>. Giza has also undergone significant expansion over recent years, and today the city, although still a suburb of Cairo, has a population of 2.7 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypop_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-citypop-158">[156]</a></sup> The Cairo Governorate was just north of the <a href="/wiki/Helwan_Governorate" title="Helwan Governorate">Helwan Governorate</a> from 2008 when some Cairo's southern districts, including <a href="/wiki/Maadi" title="Maadi">Maadi</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Cairo" title="New Cairo">New Cairo</a>, were split off and annexed into the new governorate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> to 2011 when the Helwan Governorate was reincorporated into the Cairo Governorate.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panocairo1.jpg" title="A panorama of the Nile in central Cairo showing the west side of Gezira Island, located in the middle of the Nile, with the Cairo Tower in the middle, the 6th October Bridge on the far left and El Galaa Bridge on the far right"><img alt="" data-file-height="991" data-file-width="4409" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Panocairo1.jpg/800px-Panocairo1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Panocairo1.jpg/1200px-Panocairo1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Panocairo1.jpg/1600px-Panocairo1.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panocairo1.jpg" title="File:Panocairo1.jpg"> </a></div>A panorama of the Nile in central Cairo showing the west side of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gezira_Island" title="Gezira Island">Gezira Island</a>, located in the middle of the Nile, with the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Tower" title="Cairo Tower">Cairo Tower</a> in the middle, the <a href="/wiki/6th_October_Bridge" title="6th October Bridge">6th October Bridge</a> on the far left and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Galaa_Bridge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Galaa Bridge (page does not exist)">El Galaa Bridge</a> on the far right</div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the level of air pollution in Cairo is nearly 12 times higher than the recommended safety level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Cairo, and along the Nile River Valley, the climate is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (<i>BWh</i> according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup>). Wind storms can be frequent, bringing <a href="/wiki/Mineral_dust" title="Mineral dust">Saharan dust</a> into the city, from March to May and the air often becomes uncomfortably dry. High temperatures in winter range from 14 to 22 °C (57 to 72 °F), while night-time lows drop to below 11 °C (52 °F), often to 5 °C (41 °F). In summer, the highs rarely surpass 40 °C (104 °F), and lows drop to about 20 °C (68 °F). Rainfall is sparse and only happens in the colder months, but sudden showers can cause severe flooding. The summer months have high humidity due to its coastal location. Snowfall is extremely rare; a small amount of <a href="/wiki/Graupel" title="Graupel">graupel</a>, widely believed to be <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a>, fell on Cairo's easternmost suburbs on 13 December 2013, the first time Cairo's area received this kind of precipitation in many decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> Dew points in the hottest months range from 13.9 °C (57 °F) in June to 18.3 °C (65 °F) in August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-168">[166]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_area">Metropolitan area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Metropolitan area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cairo" title="Greater Cairo">Greater Cairo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Governorate" title="Cairo Governorate">Cairo Governorate</a></div>
<p>The Greater Cairo is the largest metropolitan area in Africa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It consists of <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Governorate" title="Cairo Governorate">Cairo Governorate</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Giza_Governorate" title="Giza Governorate">Giza Governorate</a>, and parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qalyubia_Governorate" title="Qalyubia Governorate">Qalyubia Governorate</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_cities">Satellite cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Satellite cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cairo" title="Greater Cairo">Greater Cairo</a></div>
<p>Since 1977 there have been three generations of "new cities" created by the Egyptian government to accommodate additional growth and development of the Greater Cairo area, in addition to a fourth generation of new cities currently under development (including the proposed new administrative capital).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_147-3"><a href="#cite_note-:6-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> New developments include high-end residential developments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> The first generation of new cities, established between 1977 and 1982, includes <a href="/wiki/6th_of_October_(city)" title="6th of October (city)">6th of October City</a>, <a href="/wiki/10th_of_Ramadan_(city)" title="10th of Ramadan (city)">10th of Ramadan City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/15th_of_May_(city)" title="15th of May (city)">15th of May City</a>. The second generation, established between 1986 and 1997, includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badr_City" title="Badr City">Badr City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obour_(city)" title="Obour (city)">El Obour</a>. The third generation, established in the late 1990s and early 2000s (primarily between 1999 and 2000), includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Shorouk_City" title="El Shorouk City">El Shorouk City</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Cairo" title="New Cairo">New Cairo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Zayed_City" title="Sheikh Zayed City">Sheikh Zayed City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_147-4"><a href="#cite_note-:6-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-:7-148">[146]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planned_new_capital">Planned new capital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Planned new capital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_Administrative_Capital" title="New Administrative Capital">New Administrative Capital</a></div>
<p>In March 2015, plans were announced for a yet-unnamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planned_city" title="Planned city">planned city</a> to be built east of Cairo, in an undeveloped area of the Cairo Governorate, which would serve as the administrative and financial capital of Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_new_capital_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC:_new_capital-155">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Egypt" title="List of hospitals in Egypt">List of hospitals in Egypt</a></div>
<p>Cairo, as well as neighbouring Giza, has been established as Egypt's main centre for medical treatment, and despite some exceptions, has the most advanced level of <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">medical care</a> in the country. Cairo's hospitals include the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Commission" title="Joint Commission">JCI</a>-accredited As-Salaam International Hospital—Corniche El Nile, Maadi (Egypt's largest <a href="/wiki/Private_hospital" title="Private hospital">private hospital</a> with 350 beds), <a href="/wiki/Ain_Shams_University" title="Ain Shams University">Ain Shams University</a> Hospital, <a href="/wiki/Dar_Al_Fouad" title="Dar Al Fouad">Dar Al Fouad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nile_Badrawi_Hospital" title="Nile Badrawi Hospital">Nile Badrawi Hospital</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/57357_Hospital" title="57357 Hospital">57357 Hospital</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Qasr_El_Eyni_Hospital" title="Qasr El Eyni Hospital">Qasr El Eyni Hospital</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greater_Cairo" title="Greater Cairo">Greater Cairo</a> has long been the hub of education and educational services for Egypt and the region.
Today, Greater Cairo is the centre for many government offices governing the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Egypt" title="Education in Egypt">Egyptian educational system</a>, has the largest number of educational schools, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_universities" title="Egyptian universities">higher education institutes</a> among other cities and governorates of Egypt.
</p><p><b>Some of the International Schools found in Cairo:</b>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Egypt" title="List of schools in Egypt">List of schools in Egypt</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cairo" title="Transport in Cairo">Transport in Cairo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramses-Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1489" data-file-width="2633" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Ramses-Station.jpg/220px-Ramses-Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Ramses-Station.jpg/330px-Ramses-Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Ramses-Station.jpg/440px-Ramses-Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ramses-Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of <a href="/wiki/Ramses_Station" title="Ramses Station">Ramses Station</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo,_Egypt_(46845880222).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1999" data-file-width="2999" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg/220px-Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg/330px-Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg/440px-Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo,_Egypt_(46845880222).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/6th_October_Bridge" title="6th October Bridge">6th October Bridge</a> in Cairo</div></div></div>
<p>Cairo has an extensive road network, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_system" title="Rail system">rail system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subway system</a> and maritime services. Road transport is facilitated by personal vehicles, taxi cabs, privately owned public buses and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbus#Van_conversions" title="Microbus">Cairo microbuses</a>. Cairo, specifically <a href="/wiki/Ramses_Station" title="Ramses Station">Ramses Station</a>, is the centre of almost the entire Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transport_network" title="Transport network">transportation network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TravelCairo_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-TravelCairo-174">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cairo_Metro" title="Cairo Metro">The subway system</a>, officially called "Metro (مترو)", is a fast and efficient way of getting around Cairo. Metro network covers <a href="/wiki/Helwan" title="Helwan">Helwan</a> and other suburbs. It can get very crowded during <a href="/wiki/Rush_hour" title="Rush hour">rush hour</a>. Two train cars (the fourth and fifth ones) are reserved for women only, although women may ride in any car they want.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Greater_Cairo" title="Trams in Greater Cairo">Trams in Greater Cairo</a> and Cairo trolleybus were used as modes of transportation, but were closed in the 1970s everywhere except Heliopolis and Helwan. These were shut down in 2014, after the Egyptian Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>An extensive road network connects Cairo with other Egyptian cities and villages. There is a new <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">Ring Road</a> that surrounds the outskirts of the city, with exits that reach outer Cairo districts. There are flyovers and bridges, such as the <a href="/wiki/6th_October_Bridge" title="6th October Bridge">6th October Bridge</a> that, when the traffic is not heavy, allow fast<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TravelCairo_174-1"><a href="#cite_note-TravelCairo-174">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mode_of_transport" title="Mode of transport">means of transportation</a> from one side of the city to the other.
</p><p>Cairo traffic is known to be overwhelming and overcrowded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup> Traffic moves at a relatively fluid pace. Drivers tend to be aggressive, but are more courteous at junctions, taking turns going, with police aiding in <a href="/wiki/Road_traffic_control" title="Road traffic control">traffic control</a> of some congested areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TravelCairo_174-2"><a href="#cite_note-TravelCairo-174">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 plans to construct <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Monorail" title="Cairo Monorail">two monorail systems</a> were announced, one linking <a href="/wiki/6th_of_October_(city)" title="6th of October (city)">6th of October</a> to suburban <a href="/wiki/Giza" title="Giza">Giza</a>, a distance of 35 km (22 mi), and the other linking <a href="/wiki/Nasr_City" title="Nasr City">Nasr City</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_Cairo" title="New Cairo">New Cairo</a>, a distance of 52 km (32 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_forms_of_transport">Other forms of transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other forms of transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg/220px-Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg/330px-Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg/440px-Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Stadium" title="Cairo International Stadium">Cairo International Stadium</a> with 75,100 seats</div></div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Cairo%22" rel="nofollow">"Cairo"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Cairo%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Cairo%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Cairo%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Cairo%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Cairo%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Egypt,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> and Cairo has a number of sporting teams that compete in national and regional leagues most notably, <a href="/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC" title="Al Ahly SC">Al Ahly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zamalek_SC" title="Zamalek SC">Zamalek SC</a> who are the <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/CAF" title="CAF">CAF</a> first and second African clubs of the 20th century. The annual match between <a href="/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC" title="Al Ahly SC">Al Ahly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zamalek_SC" title="Zamalek SC">El Zamalek</a> is one of the most watched sports events in Egypt as well as the African-Arab region. The teams form the major rivalry of Egyptian football, and are the first and the second champions in Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>. They play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Stadium" title="Cairo International Stadium">Cairo International Stadium</a> or Naser Stadium, which is the second largest stadium in Egypt, as well as the largest in Cairo and one of the largest stadiums in the world.
</p><p>The Cairo International Stadium was built in 1960 and its multi-purpose sports complex that houses the main football stadium, an <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Stadium_Indoor_Halls_Complex" title="Cairo Stadium Indoor Halls Complex">indoor stadium</a>, several satellite fields that held several regional, continental and global games, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-Africa_Games" title="All-Africa Games">African Games</a>, U17 Football World Championship and was one of the stadiums scheduled that hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2006 Africa Cup of Nations">2006 Africa Cup of Nations</a> which was played in January 2006. Egypt later won the competition and went on to win the next edition in Ghana (2008) making the Egyptian and Ghanaian national teams the only teams to win the African Nations Cup Back to back which resulted in Egypt winning the title for a record number of six times in the history of African Continental Competition. This was followed by a third consecutive win in Angola 2010, making Egypt the only country with a record 3-consecutive and 7-total Continental Football Competition winner. This achievement had also placed the Egyptian football team as the #9 best team in the world's FIFA rankings. As of 2021, Egypt's national team is ranked at #46 in the world by FIFA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cairo failed at the applicant stage when bidding for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>, which was hosted in Beijing, China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> However, Cairo did host the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_Arab_Games" title="2007 Pan Arab Games">2007 Pan Arab Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several other sports teams in the city that participate in several sports including <a href="/wiki/Gezira_Sporting_Club" title="Gezira Sporting Club">Gezira Sporting Club</a>, el Shams Club, el Seid Club, <a href="/wiki/Heliopolis_Sporting_Club" title="Heliopolis Sporting Club">Heliopolis Sporting Club</a> and several smaller clubs, but the biggest clubs in Egypt (not in area but in sports) are <a href="/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC" title="Al Ahly SC">Al Ahly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zamalek" title="Zamalek">Al Zamalek</a>. They have the two biggest football teams in Egypt. There are new sports clubs in the area of New Cairo (one hour far from Cairo's down town), these are Al Zohour sporting club, Wadi Degla sporting club and Platinum Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the sports federations of the country are also located in the city suburbs, including the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Football_Association" title="Egyptian Football Association">Egyptian Football Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> (CAF) was previously located in Cairo, before relocating to its new headquarters in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/6th_of_October_City" title="6th of October City">6 October City</a>, a small city away from Cairo's crowded districts.
</p><p>In October 2008, the Egyptian Rugby Federation was officially formed and granted membership into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Rugby_Board" title="International Rugby Board">International Rugby Board</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>Egypt is internationally known for the excellence of its squash players who excel in both professional and junior divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> Egypt has seven players in the top ten of the PSA men's world rankings, and three in the women's top ten. Mohamed El Shorbagy held the world number one position for more than a year before being overtaken by compatriot Karim Abdel Gawad, who is number two behind Gregory Gaultier of France. Ramy Ashour and Amr Shabana are regarded as two of the most talented squash players in history. Shabana won the World Open title four times and Ashour twice, although his recent form has been hampered by injury. Egypt's Nour El Sherbini has won the Women's World Championship twice and has been women's world number one for 16 consecutive months. On 30 April 2016, she became the youngest woman to win the Women's World Championship which was held in Malaysia. In April 2017 she retained her title by winning the Women's World Championship which was held in the Egyptian resort of El Gouna.
</p><p>Cairo is the official end point of <a href="/wiki/Cross_Egypt_Challenge" title="Cross Egypt Challenge">Cross Egypt Challenge</a> where its route ends yearly in the most sacred place in Egypt, under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Pyramids_of_Giza" title="Great Pyramids of Giza">Great Pyramids of Giza</a> with a huge trophy-giving ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_Opera_House">Cairo Opera House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cairo Opera House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Opera_House" title="Cairo Opera House">Cairo Opera House</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_Mubarak" title="President Mubarak">President Mubarak</a> inaugurated the new Cairo Opera House of the Egyptian National Cultural Centres on 10 October 1988, 17 years after the Royal Opera House had been destroyed by fire. The National Cultural Centre was built with the help of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JICA" title="JICA">JICA</a>, the Japan International Co-operation Agency and stands as a prominent feature for the <a href="/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Japan_relations" title="Egypt–Japan relations">Japanese-Egyptian co-operation</a> and the friendship between the two nations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Khedivial_Opera_House">Khedivial Opera House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Khedivial Opera House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Khedivial_Opera_House" title="Khedivial Opera House">Khedivial Opera House</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Khedivial_Opera_House" title="Khedivial Opera House">Khedivial Opera House</a>, or Royal Opera House, was the original opera house in Cairo. It was dedicated on 1 November 1869 and burned down on 28 October 1971. After the original opera house was destroyed, Cairo was without an opera house for nearly two decades until the opening of the new Cairo Opera House in 1988.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_International_Film_Festival">Cairo International Film Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cairo International Film Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Film_Festival" title="Cairo International Film Festival">Cairo International Film Festival</a></div>
<p>Cairo held its first international <a href="/wiki/Film_festival" title="Film festival">film festival</a> 16 August 1976, when the first <a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Film_Festival" title="Cairo International Film Festival">Cairo International Film Festival</a> was launched by the Egyptian Association of Film Writers and Critics, headed by Kamal El-Mallakh. The Association ran the festival for seven years until 1983.
</p><p>This achievement lead to the President of the Festival again contacting the <a href="/wiki/FIAPF" title="FIAPF">FIAPF</a> with the request that a competition should be included at the 1991 Festival. The request was granted.
</p><p>In 1998, the Festival took place under the presidency of one of Egypt's leading actors, <a href="/wiki/Hussein_Fahmy" title="Hussein Fahmy">Hussein Fahmy</a>, who was appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_(Egypt)" title="Ministry of Culture (Egypt)">Minister of Culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farouk_Hosny" title="Farouk Hosny">Farouk Hosni</a>, after the death of Saad El-Din Wahba. Four years later, the journalist and writer Cherif El-Shoubashy became president.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_Geniza">Cairo Geniza</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cairo Geniza">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Schechter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="464" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solomon_Schechter.jpg/170px-Solomon_Schechter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solomon_Schechter.jpg/255px-Solomon_Schechter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Solomon_Schechter.jpg/340px-Solomon_Schechter.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solomon_Schechter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solomon Schechter studying documents from the Cairo Geniza, c. 1895.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Geniza" title="Cairo Geniza">Cairo Geniza</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Geniza" title="Cairo Geniza">Cairo Geniza</a> is an accumulation of almost 200,000 Jewish manuscripts that were found in the genizah of the <a href="/wiki/Abraham_ibn_Ezra" title="Abraham ibn Ezra">Ben Ezra</a> synagogue (built 882) of Fustat, Egypt (now Old Cairo), the Basatin cemetery east of Old Cairo, and a number of old documents that were bought in Cairo in the later 19th century. These documents were written from about 870 to 1880 AD and have been archived in various American and European libraries. The Taylor-Schechter collection in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> runs to 140,000 manuscripts; a further 40,000 manuscripts are housed at the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Theological_Seminary_of_America" title="Jewish Theological Seminary of America">Jewish Theological Seminary of America</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The majority of Cairenes make food for themselves and make use of local produce markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-189">[187]</a></sup> The restaurant scene includes <a href="/wiki/Arab_cuisine" title="Arab cuisine">Arab cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_cuisine" title="Middle Eastern cuisine">Middle Eastern cuisine</a>, including local staples such as <i><a href="/wiki/Koshary" title="Koshary">koshary</a></i>. The city's most exclusive restaurants are typically concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Zamalek" title="Zamalek">Zamalek</a> and around the luxury hotels lining the shore of the Nile near the <a href="/wiki/Garden_City,_Cairo" title="Garden City, Cairo">Garden City</a> district. Influence from modern <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">western</a> society is also evident, with American chains such as <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arby%27s" title="Arby's">Arby's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">Kentucky Fried Chicken</a> being easy to find in central areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-189">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_worship">Places of worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Places of worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mosques_in_Cairo" title="List of mosques in Cairo">List of mosques in Cairo</a></div>
<p>Among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Places_of_worship" title="Places of worship">places of worship</a>, they are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> mosques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> There are also <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> churches and temples: <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church" title="Coptic Orthodox Church">Coptic Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Catholic_Church" title="Coptic Catholic Church">Coptic Catholic Church</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>), <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_of_Egypt_(Synod_of_the_Nile)" title="Evangelical Church of Egypt (Synod of the Nile)">Evangelical Church of Egypt (Synod of the Nile)</a> (<a href="/wiki/World_Communion_of_Reformed_Churches" title="World Communion of Reformed Churches">World Communion of Reformed Churches</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg/170px-Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg/255px-Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg/340px-Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue of <a href="/wiki/Talaat_Harb" title="Talaat Harb">Talaat Pasha Harb</a>, the father of the modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_economy" title="Egyptian economy">Egyptian economy</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cairo" title="Downtown Cairo">Downtown Cairo</a></div></div></div>
<p>Cairo's economy has traditionally been based on governmental institutions and services, with the modern productive sector expanding in the 20th century to include developments in textiles and food processing - specifically the production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>. As of 2005, Egypt has the largest non-oil based GDP in the Arab world. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-191">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1894" data-file-width="3650" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG/220px-National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG/330px-National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG/440px-National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Egypt" title="National Bank of Egypt">NBE</a> towers as viewed from the Nile</div></div></div>
<p>Cairo accounts for 11% of Egypt's population and 22% of its economy (PPP). The majority of the nation's commerce is generated there, or passes through the city. The great majority of <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">publishing houses</a> and media outlets and nearly all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_studio" title="Movie studio">film studios</a> are there, as are half of the nation's hospital beds and universities. This has fuelled rapid construction in the city, with one building in five being less than 15 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-191">[189]</a></sup>
</p><p>This growth until recently surged well ahead of <a href="/wiki/Municipal_services" title="Municipal services">city services</a>. Homes, roads, electricity, telephone and sewer services were all in short supply. Analysts trying to grasp the magnitude of the change coined terms like "hyper-urbanization".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_191-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-191">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobile_manufacturers_from_Cairo">Automobile manufacturers from Cairo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Automobile manufacturers from Cairo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
