<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape_and_landmarks">Cityscape and landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cityscape and landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TahrirSQ-2020(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1957" decoding="async" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg/220px-TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg/330px-TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg/440px-TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TahrirSQ-2020(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a> (in 2020)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tahrir_Square">Tahrir Square</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tahrir Square">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a> was founded during the mid 19th century with the establishment of modern downtown Cairo. It was first named Ismailia Square, after the 19th-century ruler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khedive_Ismail" title="Khedive Ismail">Khedive Ismail</a>, who commissioned the new downtown district's 'Paris on the Nile' design. After the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1919" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1919">Egyptian Revolution of 1919</a> the square became widely known as Tahrir (Liberation) Square, though it was not officially renamed as such until after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">1952 Revolution</a> which eliminated the monarchy. Several notable buildings surround the square including, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_University_in_Cairo" title="American University in Cairo">American University in Cairo</a>'s downtown campus, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mogamma" title="Mogamma">Mogamma</a> governmental administrative Building, the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the Nile Ritz Carlton Hotel, and the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Egyptian Museum</a>. Being at the heart of Cairo, the square witnessed several major protests over the years. However, the most notable event in the square was being the focal point of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Egyptian_Revolution" title="2011 Egyptian Revolution">2011 Egyptian Revolution</a> against former president <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> In 2020 the government completed the erection of a new monument in the center of the square featuring an ancient <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisk</a> from the reign of <a href="/wiki/Ramesses_II" title="Ramesses II">Ramses II</a>, originally unearthed at <a href="/wiki/Tanis" title="Tanis">Tanis</a> (San al-Hagar) in 2019, and four ram-headed <a href="/wiki/Sphinx" title="Sphinx">sphinx</a> statues moved from <a href="/wiki/Karnak" title="Karnak">Karnak</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-200">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_Museum">Egyptian Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Egyptian Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3421" data-file-width="4561" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg/220px-Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg/330px-Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg/440px-Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main entrance of the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Egyptian Museum</a>, located at Tahrir Square</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Museum" title="Egyptian Museum">Museum of Egyptian Antiquities</a>, known commonly as the Egyptian Museum, is home to the most extensive collection of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egyptian</a> antiquities in the world. It has 136,000 items on display, with many more hundreds of thousands in its basement storerooms. Among the collections on display are the finds from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KV62" title="KV62">tomb of Tutankhamun</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Egyptian_Museum">Grand Egyptian Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Grand Egyptian Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grand_Egyptian_Museum" title="Grand Egyptian Museum">Grand Egyptian Museum</a></div>
<p>Much of the collection of the Museum of Egyptian Antiquities, including the Tutankhamun collection, are slated to be moved to the new <a href="/wiki/Grand_Egyptian_Museum" title="Grand Egyptian Museum">Grand Egyptian Museum</a>, under construction in <a href="/wiki/Giza" title="Giza">Giza</a> and was due to open by the end of 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cairo_Tower">Cairo Tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cairo Tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Tower" title="Cairo Tower">Cairo Tower</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairotower.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cairotower.jpg/170px-Cairotower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cairotower.jpg/255px-Cairotower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cairotower.jpg/340px-Cairotower.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairotower.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cairo_Tower" title="Cairo Tower">Cairo Tower</a> at night</div></div></div>
<p>The Cairo Tower is a free-standing tower with a revolving restaurant at the top. It provides a bird's eye view of Cairo to the restaurant patrons. It stands in the Zamalek district on Gezira Island in the Nile River, in the city centre. At 187 m (614 ft), it is 44 m (144 ft) higher than the Great Pyramid of Giza, which stands some 15 km (9 mi) to the southwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Cairo">Old Cairo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Old Cairo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Old_Cairo" title="Old Cairo">Old Cairo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg/220px-Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg/330px-Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg/440px-Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hanging_Church" title="Hanging Church">Hanging Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_Cairo" title="Old Cairo">Old Cairo</a></div></div></div>
<p>This area of Cairo is so-named as it contains the remains of the ancient Roman fortress of Babylon and also overlaps the original site of <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">Fustat</a>, the first Arab settlement in Egypt (7th century AD) and the predecessor of later Cairo. The area includes the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Cairo" title="Coptic Cairo">Coptic Cairo</a>, which holds a high concentration of old Christian churches such as the <a href="/wiki/Hanging_Church" title="Hanging Church">Hanging Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._George_(Cairo)" title="Church of St. George (Cairo)">Greek Orthodox Church of St. George</a>, and other Christian or Coptic buildings, most of which are located over the site of the ancient Roman fortress. It is also the location of the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Museum" title="Coptic Museum">Coptic Museum</a>, which showcases the history of <a href="/wiki/Coptic_art" title="Coptic art">Coptic art</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egypt_history#Ptolemaic_and_Roman_Egypt" title="Egypt history">Greco-Roman</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Muslim_Egypt" title="History of Muslim Egypt">Islamic</a> times, and of the <a href="/wiki/Ben_Ezra_Synagogue" title="Ben Ezra Synagogue">Ben Ezra Synagogue</a>, the oldest and best-known <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a> in Cairo, where the important collection of <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Geniza" title="Cairo Geniza">Geniza documents</a> were discovered in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200843_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200843-207">[205]</a></sup> To the north of this Coptic enclave is the Amr ibn al-'As Mosque, the first mosque in Egypt and the most important religious centre of what was formerly <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">Fustat</a>, founded in 642 AD right after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_conquest_of_Egypt" title="Arab conquest of Egypt">Arab conquest</a> but rebuilt many times since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200839_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200839-208">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_Cairo">Islamic Cairo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Islamic Cairo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg/220px-El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg/330px-El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg/440px-El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Muizz_Street" title="Muizz Street">Al-Muizz Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a></div></div></div>
<p>Cairo holds one of the greatest concentrations of historical monuments of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(March_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_209-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(March_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-209'>[207]</a></sup> The areas around the old <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_architecture#Cairo_fortifications" title="Fatimid architecture">walled</a> city and around the Citadel are characterized by hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mosques" title="Mosques">mosques</a>, tombs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrasas" title="Madrasas">madrasas</a>, mansions, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caravanserais" title="Caravanserais">caravanserais</a>, and fortifications dating from the Islamic era and are often referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Islamic_Cairo" title="Islamic Cairo">Islamic Cairo</a>", especially in English travel literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> It is also the location of several important religious shrines such as the <a href="/wiki/Al-Hussein_Mosque" title="Al-Hussein Mosque">al-Hussein Mosque</a> (whose shrine is believed to hold the head of <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn ibn Ali</a>), the Mausoleum of Imam <a href="/wiki/Al-Shafi%27i" title="Al-Shafi'i">al-Shafi'i</a> (founder of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Madhhab" title="Madhhab">madhhab</a></i>, one of the primary schools of thought in Sunni Islamic <a href="/wiki/Fiqh" title="Fiqh">jurisprudence</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Mashhad_of_Sayyida_Ruqayya" title="Mashhad of Sayyida Ruqayya">Tomb of Sayyida Ruqayya</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Sayeda_Nafeesah_Mosque" title="Al-Sayeda Nafeesah Mosque">Mosque of Sayyida Nafisa</a>, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008-211">[209]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-Azhar_(inside)_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg/220px-Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg/330px-Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg/440px-Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-Azhar_(inside)_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Al-Azhar Mosque, view of Fatimid-era courtyard and Mamluk minarets</div></div></div>
<p>The first mosque in Egypt was the Mosque of Amr ibn al-As in what was formerly Fustat, the first Arab-Muslim settlement in the area. However, the Mosque of Ibn Tulun is the oldest mosque that still retains its original form and is a rare example of Abbasid architecture from the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">classical period of Islamic civilization</a>. It was built in 876–879 AD in a style inspired by the Abbasid capital of <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">Samarra</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850–54_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850–54-212">[210]</a></sup> It is one of the largest mosques in Cairo and is often cited as one of the most beautiful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850-213">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201287_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201287-214">[212]</a></sup> Another Abbasid construction, the <a href="/wiki/Nilometer" title="Nilometer">Nilometer</a> on Roda Island, is the oldest original structure in Cairo, built in 862 AD. It was designed to measure the level of the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>, which was important for agricultural and administrative purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>The settlement that was formally named Cairo (Arabic: <i>al-Qahira</i>) was founded to the northeast of Fustat in 959 AD by the victorious Fatimid army. The Fatimids built it as a separate palatial city which contained <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Great_Palaces" title="Fatimid Great Palaces">their palaces</a> and institutions of government. It was enclosed by a circuit of walls, which were rebuilt in stone in the late 11th century AD by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vizir" title="Vizir">vizir</a> <a href="/wiki/Badr_al-Jamali" title="Badr al-Jamali">Badr al-Gamali</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond199362_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199362-216">[214]</a></sup> parts of which survive today at Bab Zuwayla in the south and Bab al-Futuh and Bab al-Nasr in the north. Among the extant monuments from the Fatimid era are the large <a href="/wiki/Al-Hakim_Mosque" title="Al-Hakim Mosque">Mosque of al-Hakim</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aqmar_Mosque" title="Aqmar Mosque">Aqmar Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juyushi_Mosque" title="Juyushi Mosque">Juyushi Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lulua_Mosque" title="Lulua Mosque">Lulua Mosque</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Al-Salih_Tala%27i_Mosque" title="Al-Salih Tala'i Mosque">Mosque of Al-Salih Tala'i</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199258–77_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199258–77-217">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008-211">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the most important and lasting institutions founded in the Fatimid period was the Mosque of al-Azhar, founded in 970 AD, which competes with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qarawiyyin" title="Qarawiyyin">Qarawiyyin</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fes" title="Fes">Fes</a> for the title of oldest university in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169-218">[216]</a></sup> Today, al-Azhar University is the foremost Center of Islamic learning in the world and one of Egypt's largest universities with campuses across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169-218">[216]</a></sup> The mosque itself retains significant Fatimid elements but has been added to and expanded in subsequent centuries, notably by the Mamluk sultans Qaytbay and al-Ghuri and by Abd al-Rahman Katkhuda in the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199262_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199262-219">[217]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg/220px-%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg/330px-%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg/440px-%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mosque-Madrasa_of_Sultan_Hassan" title="Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hassan">Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hassan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Al-Rifa%27i_Mosque" title="Al-Rifa'i Mosque">al-Rifa'i Mosque</a>, seen from the Citadel</div></div></div>
<p>The most prominent architectural heritage of medieval Cairo, however, dates from the Mamluk period, from 1250 to 1517 AD. The Mamluk sultans and elites were eager patrons of religious and scholarly life, commonly building religious or funerary complexes whose functions could include a mosque, madrasa, <a href="/wiki/Khanqah" title="Khanqah">khanqah</a> (for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufis" title="Sufis">Sufis</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Sebil_(fountain)" title="Sebil (fountain)">sabil</a> (water dispensary), and a mausoleum for themselves and their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-80">[78]</a></sup> Among the best-known examples of Mamluk monuments in Cairo are the huge Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hasan, the <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Amir_al-Maridani" title="Mosque of Amir al-Maridani">Mosque of Amir al-Maridani</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Sultan_al-Muayyad" title="Mosque of Sultan al-Muayyad">Mosque of Sultan al-Mu'ayyad</a> (whose twin minarets were built above the gate of Bab Zuwayla), the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Al-Ghuri_Complex" title="Sultan Al-Ghuri Complex">Sultan Al-Ghuri complex</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Complex_of_Sultan_al-Ashraf_Qaytbay" title="Complex of Sultan al-Ashraf Qaytbay">funerary complex of Sultan Qaytbay</a> in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_the_Dead_(Cairo)" title="City of the Dead (Cairo)">Northern Cemetery</a>, and the trio of monuments in the <a href="/wiki/Bayn_al-Qasrayn" title="Bayn al-Qasrayn">Bayn al-Qasrayn</a> area comprising the <a href="/wiki/Qalawun_complex" title="Qalawun complex">complex of Sultan al-Mansur Qalawun</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrassa_of_Al-Nasir_Muhammad" title="Madrassa of Al-Nasir Muhammad">Madrasa of al-Nasir Muhammad</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrasa_of_Sultan_Barquq" title="Madrasa of Sultan Barquq">Madrasa of Sultan Barquq</a>. Some mosques include <a href="/wiki/Spolia" title="Spolia">spolia</a> (often columns or <a href="/wiki/Capital_(architecture)" title="Capital (architecture)">capitals</a>) from earlier buildings built by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Copts" title="Copts">Copts</a>.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(March_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_209-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(March_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-209'>[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mamluks, and the later Ottomans, also built <i>wikala</i>s or caravanserais to house merchants and goods due to the important role of trade and commerce in Cairo's economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97-220">[218]</a></sup> Still intact today is the <a href="/wiki/Wikala_of_Al-Ghuri" title="Wikala of Al-Ghuri">Wikala al-Ghuri</a>, which today hosts regular performances by the Al-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tannoura" title="Tannoura">Tannoura</a> Egyptian Heritage Dance Troupe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201281_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201281-221">[219]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili" title="Khan el-Khalili">Khan al-Khalili</a> is a commercial hub which also integrated caravanserais (also known as <i>khan</i>s).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-:13-222">[220]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citadel_of_Cairo">Citadel of Cairo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Citadel of Cairo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_(4).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2380" data-file-width="3896" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_%284%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_%284%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_%284%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_(4).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Citadel of Cairo, with the <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Muhammad_Ali" title="Mosque of Muhammad Ali">Mosque of Muhammad Ali</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Citadel" title="Cairo Citadel">Cairo Citadel</a></div>
<p>The Citadel is a fortified enclosure begun by <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Salah al-Din</a> in 1176 AD on an outcrop of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muqatam" title="Muqatam">Muqattam Hills</a> as part of a large defensive system to protect both Cairo to the north and <a href="/wiki/Fustat" title="Fustat">Fustat</a> to the southwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97-220">[218]</a></sup> It was the centre of Egyptian government and residence of its rulers until 1874, when <a href="/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha" title="Isma'il Pasha">Khedive Isma'il</a> moved to <a href="/wiki/Abdeen_Palace" title="Abdeen Palace">'Abdin Palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008221_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008221-223">[221]</a></sup> It is still occupied by the military today, but is now open as a tourist attraction comprising, notably, the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_National_Military_Museum" title="Egyptian National Military Museum">National Military Museum</a>, the 14th century <a href="/wiki/Al-Nasir_Muhammad_Mosque" title="Al-Nasir Muhammad Mosque">Mosque of al-Nasir Muhammad</a>, and the 19th century <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Muhammad_Ali" title="Mosque of Muhammad Ali">Mosque of Muhammad Ali</a> which commands a dominant position on Cairo's skyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2018259–272_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2018259–272-224">[222]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Khan_el-Khalili">Khan el-Khalili</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Khan el-Khalili">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili" title="Khan el-Khalili">Khan el-Khalili</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khan_el-Khalili,_Old_Cairo,_al-Q%C4%81hirah,_CG,_EGY_(40944894033).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg/220px-Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg/330px-Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg/440px-Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khan_el-Khalili,_Old_Cairo,_al-Q%C4%81hirah,_CG,_EGY_(40944894033).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A medieval gateway in <a href="/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili" title="Khan el-Khalili">Khan al-Khalili</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili" title="Khan el-Khalili">Khan el-Khalili</a> is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a>, or marketplace adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Al-Hussein_Mosque" title="Al-Hussein Mosque">Al-Hussein Mosque</a>. It dates back to 1385, when Amir Jarkas el-Khalili built a large caravanserai, or khan. (A caravanserai is a hotel for traders, and usually the focal point for any surrounding area.) This original carvanserai building was demolished by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qansuh_al-Ghuri" title="Qansuh al-Ghuri">Sultan al-Ghuri</a>, who rebuilt it as a new commercial complex in the early 16th century, forming the basis for the network of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Souqs" title="Souqs">souqs</a> existing today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaymond1993179_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond1993179-225">[223]</a></sup> Many medieval elements remain today, including the ornate <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluk</a>-style gateways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008179_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008179-226">[224]</a></sup> Today, the Khan el-Khalili is a major tourist attraction and popular stop for tour groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201274–75_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201274–75-227">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the present day, Cairo is heavily <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanized</a> and most Cairenes live in apartment buildings. Because of the influx of people into the city, lone standing houses are rare, and apartment buildings accommodate for the limited space and abundance of people. Single detached houses are usually owned by the wealthy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-february_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-february-228">[226]</a></sup> Formal education is also seen as important, with twelve years of standard formal education. Cairenes can take a standardized test similar to the <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> to be accepted to an institution of higher learning, but most children do not finish school and opt to pick up a trade to enter the work force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-february_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-february-228">[226]</a></sup> Egypt still struggles with <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, with almost half the population living on $2 or less a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Women.27s_rights"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_rights">Women's rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Women's rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Egypt" title="Women in Egypt">Women in Egypt</a></div>
<p>The civil rights movement for women in Cairo - and by extent, Egypt - has been a struggle for years. Women are reported to face constant discrimination, sexual harassment, and abuse throughout Cairo. A 2013 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> study found that over 99% of <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Egypt" title="Women in Egypt">Egyptian women</a> reported experiencing sexual harassment at some point in their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup> The problem has persisted in spite of new national laws since 2014 defining and criminalizing sexual harassment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup> The situation is so severe that in 2017, Cairo was named by one poll as the most dangerous <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> for women in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> In 2020, the social media account "Assault Police" began to name and shame perpetrators of violence against women, in an effort to dissuade potential offenders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> The account was founded by student <a href="/wiki/Nadeen_Ashraf" title="Nadeen Ashraf">Nadeen Ashraf</a>, who is credited for instigating an iteration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Me_Too_movement" title="Me Too movement">#MeToo movement</a> in Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution">Pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> in Cairo is a matter of serious concern. Greater Cairo's volatile <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aromatic_hydrocarbon" title="Aromatic hydrocarbon">aromatic hydrocarbon</a> levels are higher than many other similar cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> Air quality measurements in Cairo have also been recording dangerous levels of <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulphur dioxide</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Suspended_solids" title="Suspended solids">suspended particulate matter</a> concentrations due to decades of unregulated <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_emissions_control" title="Vehicle emissions control">vehicle emissions</a>, urban industrial operations, and chaff and trash burning. There are over 4,500,000 cars on the streets of Cairo, 60% of which are over 10 years old, and therefore lack modern emission cutting features. Cairo has a very poor dispersion factor because of its lack of rain and its layout of tall buildings and narrow streets, which create a bowl effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NilPollution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NilPollution.jpg/220px-NilPollution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NilPollution.jpg/330px-NilPollution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NilPollution.jpg/440px-NilPollution.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NilPollution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Smog in Cairo</div></div></div>
<p>In recent years, a black cloud (as Egyptians refer to it) of <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a>  has appeared over Cairo every autumn due to <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">temperature inversion</a>. Smog causes serious respiratory diseases and eye irritations for the city's citizens. Tourists who are not familiar with such high levels of pollution must take extra care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cairo also has many unregistered lead and <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smelter" title="Smelter">smelters</a> which heavily pollute the city. The results of this has been a permanent haze over the city with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate_matter" title="Particulate matter">particulate matter</a> in the air reaching over three times normal levels. It is estimated that 10,000 to 25,000 people a year in Cairo die due to air pollution-related diseases. Lead has been shown to cause harm to the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> and neurotoxicity particularly in children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup> In 1995, the first environmental acts were introduced and the situation has seen some improvement with 36 air monitoring stations and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emissions_testing" title="Emissions testing">emissions tests</a> on cars. Twenty thousand buses have also been commissioned to the city to improve congestion levels, which are very high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Traffic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cairo_Traffic.jpg/220px-Cairo_Traffic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cairo_Traffic.jpg/330px-Cairo_Traffic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cairo_Traffic.jpg/440px-Cairo_Traffic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cairo_Traffic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traffic in Cairo</div></div></div>
<p>The city also suffers from a high level of land pollution. Cairo produces 10,000 tons of waste material each day, 4,000 tons of which is not <a href="/wiki/Waste_collection" title="Waste collection">collected</a> or <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">managed</a>. This is a huge health hazard, and the Egyptian Government is looking for ways to combat this. The Cairo Cleaning and Beautification Agency was founded to collect and recycle the waste; they work with the <a href="/wiki/Zabbaleen" title="Zabbaleen">Zabbaleen</a>  community that has been collecting and recycling Cairo's waste since the turn of the 20th century and live in an area known locally as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manshiyat_naser" title="Manshiyat naser">Manshiyat naser</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> Both are working together to pick up as much waste as possible within the city limits, though it remains a pressing problem.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">Water pollution</a> is also a serious problem in the city as the <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">sewer system</a> tends to fail and overflow. On occasion, <a href="/wiki/Sewage" title="Sewage">sewage</a> has escaped onto the streets to create a health hazard. This problem is hoped to be solved by a new sewer system funded by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, which could cope with the demand of the city. The dangerously high levels of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a> in the city's water system has <a href="/wiki/Global_health" title="Global health">global health</a> officials concerned over related health risks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_Arab_League" title="Headquarters of the Arab League">Headquarters of the Arab League</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cairo" title="Downtown Cairo">downtown business district</a> of Cairo.
</p>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gamal_Aziz" title="Gamal Aziz">Gamal Aziz</a>, also known as Gamal Mohammed Abdelaziz, former president and chief operating officer of <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Resorts" title="Wynn Resorts">Wynn Resorts</a>, and former CEO of <a href="/wiki/MGM_Resorts_International" title="MGM Resorts International">MGM Resorts International</a>, indicted as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019_college_admissions_bribery_scandal" title="2019 college admissions bribery scandal">2019 college admissions bribery scandal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> (4/ 24 August 1929 – 11 November 2004) Born <i>Mohammed Abdel Rahman Abdel Raouf al-Qudwa al-Husseini</i> was the 3rd Chairman of The <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">PLO</a> and first president of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian Authority</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Abu_Sa%27id_al-Afif" title="Abu Sa'id al-Afif">Abu Sa'id al-Afif</a>, 15th-century Samaritan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boutros_Boutros-Ghali" title="Boutros Boutros-Ghali">Boutros Ghali</a> (1922–2016), former <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Avi_Cohen" title="Avi Cohen">Avi Cohen</a> (1956–2010), Israeli international footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dalida" title="Dalida">Dalida</a> (1933–1987), Italian-Egyptian singer who lived most of her life in France, received 55 golden records and was the first singer to receive a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">diamond disc</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Farouk_El-Baz" title="Farouk El-Baz">Farouk El-Baz</a> (born 1938), an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_American" title="Egyptian American">Egyptian American</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_scientist" title="Space scientist">space scientist</a> who worked with <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> to assist in the planning of scientific exploration of the Moon, including the selection of landing sites for the Apollo missions and the training of astronauts in lunar observations and photography.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mohamed_ElBaradei" title="Mohamed ElBaradei">Mohamed ElBaradei</a> (born 1942), former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Director-general" title="Director-general">Director General</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">2005 Nobel Peace Prize laureate</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nourane_Fotsing_Moluh_Hassana" title="Nourane Fotsing Moluh Hassana">Nourane Foster</a> (born 1987), Cameroonian entrepreneur, politician, and member of the National Assembly.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mauro_Hamza" title="Mauro Hamza">Mauro Hamza</a>, fencing coach</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Zulfikar" title="Ahmed Zulfikar">Ahmed Zulfikar</a> (15 August 1952 – 1 May 2010) was an Egyptian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineer" title="Mechanical engineer">mechanical engineer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entrepreneur" title="Entrepreneur">entrepreneur</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taco_Hemingway" title="Taco Hemingway">Taco Hemingway</a> (born 1990), Polish hip-hop artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Hodgkin" title="Dorothy Hodgkin">Dorothy Hodgkin</a> (1910–1994), British chemist, credited with the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protein_crystallography" title="Protein crystallography">protein crystallography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a> in 1964</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a> (15 January 1918 – 28 September 1970) was an Egyptian politician who served as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Egypt" title="List of Presidents of Egypt">second President of Egypt</a> from 1954 until his death in 1970.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yakub_Kadri_Karaosmano%C4%9Flu" title="Yakub Kadri Karaosmanoğlu">Yakub Kadri Karaosmanoğlu</a> (1889–1974), Turkish novelist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mona_Zulficar" title="Mona Zulficar">Mona Zulficar</a> (born 1950) <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptian</a> <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">lawyer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_rights_activist" title="Human rights activist">human rights activist</a> and was included in the <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> 2021 list of the "100 most powerful businesswomen in the Arab region"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naguib_Mahfouz" title="Naguib Mahfouz">Naguib Mahfouz</a> (1911–2006), novelist, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1988</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roland_Moreno" title="Roland Moreno">Roland Moreno</a> (1945–2012), French inventor, engineer, humorist and author who invented the <a href="/wiki/Smart_card" title="Smart card">smart card</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaafar_Nimeiry" title="Gaafar Nimeiry">Gaafar Nimeiry</a> (1930–2009), President of Sudan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Sabri" title="Ahmed Sabri">Ahmed Sabri</a> (1889–1955), painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hesham_Youssef" title="Hesham Youssef">Hesham Youssef</a>, Egyptian diplomat</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ezz_El-Dine_Zulficar" title="Ezz El-Dine Zulficar">Ezz El-Dine Zulficar</a>, (October 28, 1919 – July 1, 1963) was an <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptian</a> film director, screenwriter, actor and producer. known for his distinctive style, which blends romance and action. Zulficar was one of the most influential filmmakers in the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Egypt" title="Cinema of Egypt">Egyptian Cinema's</a> golden age</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naguib_Sawiris" title="Naguib Sawiris">Naguib Sawiris</a> (born 1954), Egyptian businessman, 62nd richest person on Earth in 2007 <a href="/wiki/Billionaire" title="Billionaire">list of billionaires</a>, reaching US$10.0 billion with his company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orascom_Telecom_Holding" title="Orascom Telecom Holding">Orascom Telecom Holding</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Sobhi_(actor)" title="Mohamed Sobhi (actor)">Mohamed Sobhi</a> (born 1948), Egyptian film, television and stage actor, director</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">Blessed</a> <a href="/wiki/Maria_Caterina_Troiani" title="Maria Caterina Troiani">Maria Caterina Troiani</a> (1813–1887), a <a href="/wiki/Mercy" title="Mercy">charitable activist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Magdi_Yacoub" title="Magdi Yacoub">Magdi Yacoub</a> (born 1935), Egyptian-British cardiothoracic surgeon</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cairo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cairo Metropolitan is enlarged to cover all the area within the Governorate limits. Government statistics consider that the whole governorate is urban and the whole governorate is treated like as the metropolitan-city of Cairo. Governorate Cairo is considered a city-proper and functions as a municipality. The city of Alexandria is on the same principle as the city of Cairo, being a governorate-city. Because of this, it is difficult to divide Cairo into urban, rural, subdivisions, or to eliminate certain parts of the metropolitan administrative territory on various theme (unofficial statistics and data).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The historical chronicler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_of_Nikiou" title="John of Nikiou">John of Nikiou</a> attributed the construction of the fortress to Trajan, but more recent excavations date the fortress to the time of Diocletian. A succession of canals connecting the Nile Valley with the Red Sea were also previously dug around this region in different periods prior to Trajan. Trajan's canal fell out of use some time between the reign of Diocletian and the 7th century.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
